<div id="review_596537916" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/596537916" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2473504-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1394406877p2/2473504.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/596537916?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/2473504-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=listened-to-audiobook">listened-to-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=stand-alone-novel">stand-alone-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=womens-fiction-chicklit">womens-fiction-chicklit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=book-to-screen">book-to-screen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=epistolary-novel">epistolary-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer596537916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2344065735419540377"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/147865.Love__Rosie' title='Love, Rosie by Cecelia Ahern' rel='nofollow noopener'>Love, Rosie</a> is a standalone, chick-lit/women’s fiction novel written by author <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7116.Cecelia_Ahern' title='Cecelia Ahern' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cecelia Ahern</a>. I LOVED this book! The writing style is delightful as every character and event in this story is brought to the reader through a chronological compilation of text messages, message board posts, emails, letters, instant messaging, etc. An entire book told through correspondence??? I questioned it too, but believe me, it works!!! I fell in love with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/147865.Love__Rosie' title='Love, Rosie by Cecelia Ahern' rel='nofollow noopener'>Love, Rosie</a> pretty much immediately and devoured every a</span>
  <span id="freeText2344065735419540377" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/147865.Love__Rosie" title="Love, Rosie by Cecelia Ahern" rel="nofollow noopener">Love, Rosie</a> is a standalone, chick-lit/women’s fiction novel written by author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7116.Cecelia_Ahern" title="Cecelia Ahern" rel="nofollow noopener">Cecelia Ahern</a>. I LOVED this book! The writing style is delightful as every character and event in this story is brought to the reader through a chronological compilation of text messages, message board posts, emails, letters, instant messaging, etc. An entire book told through correspondence??? I questioned it too, but believe me, it works!!! I fell in love with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/147865.Love__Rosie" title="Love, Rosie by Cecelia Ahern" rel="nofollow noopener">Love, Rosie</a> pretty much immediately and devoured every adorable page. Now, I’m not saying it’s all drama-free bliss. It’s not...and I felt it. The moral of this story is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[LIFE IS SHORT! If you want someone in your life, you have to have the courage to communicate it! If you have a dream to fulfill, don't wait! Be brave- you never know where life will take you (or where it will keep you)! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I grew increasingly frustrated with the two main characters: Rosie and Alex and their choices in this matter, but this just attests to how this story was able to keep me invested and engaged, which again is quite an accomplishment given the correspondence theme. If you need some stress relief and think you can enjoy a romantic comedy that is bound to be a classic, then try out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/147865.Love__Rosie" title="Love, Rosie by Cecelia Ahern" rel="nofollow noopener">Love, Rosie</a>!<br /><br /><b>My favorite quote:</b><br /><i>“Our life is made up of time; our days are measured in hours, our pay measured by those hours, our knowledge is measured by years. We grab a few quick minutes in our busy day to have a coffee break. We rush back to our desks, we watch the clock, we live by appointments. And yet your time eventually runs out and you wonder in your heart of hearts if those seconds, minutes, hours, days, weeks, months, years and decades were being spent the best way they possibly could. In other words, if you could change anything, would you?”</i><br /><br /><b>Tidbits:</b><br />This book has been published under several different titles, but to my knowledge, they are all the same story:<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/147865.Love__Rosie" title="Love, Rosie by Cecelia Ahern" rel="nofollow noopener">Love, Rosie</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/714985.Where_Rainbows_End" title="Where Rainbows End by Cecelia Ahern" rel="nofollow noopener">Where Rainbows End</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8949535.Rosie_Dunne" title="Rosie Dunne by Cecelia Ahern" rel="nofollow noopener">Rosie Dunne</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12363782.Soulmates" title="Soulmates by Cecelia Ahern" rel="nofollow noopener">Soulmates</a><br /> <br />Guess what?? <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/147865.Love__Rosie" title="Love, Rosie by Cecelia Ahern" rel="nofollow noopener">Love, Rosie</a> has been adapted to film! I think release dates may vary per country, but if you're interested, check out the movie trailer <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=SqSE6Kzuht0" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>!<br /><br />Note: I listened to the audiobook version, and not long after starting, I had planned to switch from audio to the page when I realized how this story was set up. But since I already had access to the audio and I would have to wait a while for a copy of the paper book, I decided to give the audio a try anyways. In the audio, each character is presented in a different voice and it became easy to keep track of all the characters while filtering through the letters, messages, etc. Also, each message has its own introduction to avoid confusion with timeframes, characters, etc. I actually found the audio to be a great experience, although I can’t actually compare the two.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2344065735419540377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Coreen ❇" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43075248-coreen"><img alt="Coreen ❇" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604385336p2/43075248.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1488378523?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Coreen ❇" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Coreen ❇" href="/user/show/43075248-coreen">Coreen ❇</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1488378523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17070429917450463119"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I've learned that home isn't a place, it's a feeling."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>This is one of those rare instances where the movie is better than the book. I don’t mean to be rude, but this is just a bunch of clusterfucked notes and emails from two people who are too scared to tell what they feel for each other, so they ended up losing decades of their lives.<br/><blockquote>
<b><u>Ready Player One</u></b> movie adaptation is a shitfest.<br/><b><u>The Lightning Thief</u></b> movie adaptation was butchered.<br/><b><u>Love, Rosie</u></b> movie adaptation turned out to be a lot</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText17070429917450463119" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I've learned that home isn't a place, it's a feeling."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This is one of those rare instances where the movie is better than the book. I don’t mean to be rude, but this is just a bunch of clusterfucked notes and emails from two people who are too scared to tell what they feel for each other, so they ended up losing decades of their lives.<br><blockquote>
<b><u>Ready Player One</u></b> movie adaptation is a shitfest.<br><b><u>The Lightning Thief</u></b> movie adaptation was butchered.<br><b><u>Love, Rosie</u></b> movie adaptation turned out to be a lot better than the book!</blockquote><br> I think seeing the movie before reading the book is one the main reasons as to why I am vastly disappointed when I finally decided to read the novel. Maybe it’s just the format or the writing style but I absolutely abhor <i>Love, Rosie</i>. The characters are flat! It’s like floating in a sea full of paper dolls. They are too fucking lifeless and I actually found myself rolling my eyes so hard I almost went blind to the amount of bullshit and beating around the bush written on this book.<br><br>Reading the physical copy of this story turned out to be a lot of work for me because I get extremely bored most the time and I am not someone who do not finish things that I started, so I switched to the audiobook and thank goodness because the narrator/s are good. Suffice it to say that I did not like the novel, but I liked the audiobook and I freaking adored the movie so much that I watched it 11 times now!<br>This is one of those rare instances where the movie is better than the book. I don’t mean to be rude, but this is just a bunch of clusterfucked notes and emails from two people who are too scared to tell what they feel for each other, so they ended up losing decades of their lives.<br><br><b>Ready Player One</b> movie adaptation is a shitfest.<br><b>The Lightning Thief</b> movie adaptation was butchered.<br><b>Love, Rosie</b> movie adaptation turned out to be a lot better than the book!<br><br> I think seeing the movie before reading the book is one the main reasons as to why I am vastly disappointed when I finally decided to read the novel. Maybe it’s just the format or the writing style but I absolutely abhor <i>Love, Rosie</i>. The characters are flat! It’s like floating in a sea full of paper dolls. They are too fucking lifeless and I actually found myself rolling my eyes so hard I almost went blind to the amount of bullshit and beating around the bush written on this book.<br><br>Reading the physical copy of this story turned out to be a lot of work for me because I get extremely bored most the time and I am not someone who do not finish things that I started, so I switched to the audiobook and thank goodness because the narrator/s are good. Suffice it to say that I did not like the novel, but I liked the audiobook and I freaking adored the movie so much that I watched it 11 times now!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1482923469p8/1793410.jpg" width="300" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_5440088" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5440088" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/294108-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1187723397p2/294108.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5440088?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/294108-amanda">Amanda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5440088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6475427020995712646">OK, this book was such a quick read, and funny, funny, FUNNY! It’s not your typical book…it is like a large scrap book of letters, emails and instant messages… between two best friends (boy and girl). The whole book you are laughing and crying and angry because they are silly, and just destined to be together… and they have a hard time realizing that... and well, it’s just great. The only reason It’s not a 5 star… is because of some language choices the author made… not cool. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <i>Home isn't a place, its a feeling.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/>This is one of those books that, ever since it first came out, no matter if I already know how it ends or if it's not my favorite book on the list, I always come back and reread from time to time.<br/>It's one of those books I like to call <b>mood reads</b> because you don't read it because you want to, you read it because you feel it's the right thing to do in that moment. <br/><br/>Where Rainbows End, or <i>Love, Rosie</i> as you want to call it, is a <s>bitter</s>sweet and funny journey thr</span>
  <span id="freeText8180565138899809306" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Home isn't a place, its a feeling.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><br>This is one of those books that, ever since it first came out, no matter if I already know how it ends or if it's not my favorite book on the list, I always come back and reread from time to time.<br>It's one of those books I like to call <b>mood reads</b> because you don't read it because you want to, you read it because you feel it's the right thing to do in that moment. <br><br>Where Rainbows End, or <i>Love, Rosie</i> as you want to call it, is a <s>bitter</s>sweet and funny journey through Alex and Rosie's lives, a book-long letter to a distant relative and a fantastic hymn to friendship in all its shapes. <br>I absolutely adore the format (I've yet to find another book that has this kind of epistolary route so if you have any recs please feel free to hit me up!), and the way every detail is revealed is just genius.<br>I love Rosie's friendship with Ruby and her relationship with her daughter. I haven't thought about it till now, but she's the kind of mother I aspire to be.<br>And Alex is just great. I wish I had his dedication. <br>He and Rosie are just...ahdhsbsubejebeh.<br>Let's just say I still obsess over their <i>silence</i> till this day. <br><br>Thia book makes me all nostalgic and brings me back happy memories, even if I'm not someone who likes to brag or cry about the past. If I think about its ending, I get all squishy and warm, too. <br>Acrually... <br>You know what? I think it's time for a reread!<br><br>{In case anyone is asking, and even if you're not let me tell you anyway, I've seen the movie and I liked it even if it was a bit different. And I absolutely loved Lily and Sam as Rosie and Alex.}<br><br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/3OLi" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2491507618?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aishu Rehman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aishu Rehman" href="/user/show/73221135-aishu-rehman">Aishu Rehman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316295796" href="/book/show/20706297-love-rosie">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73221135-aishu-rehman?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73221135-aishu-rehman?shelf=english-literature">english-literature</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2491507618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8139598480970278078">I was as frustrated by this book as I was addicted to it. Rosie and Alex were always in love with each other but never at the right place at the right time, both emotionally and physically. And neither would admit their feelings. I tore through the pages muttering under my breath that if the author did not make things right EVENTUALLY, I would lose it. I won't give anything away.<br/><br/>I thought it was adorable that Rosie's daughter Katie had a relationship with a boy named Toby that completed mirrored</span>
  <span id="freeText8139598480970278078" style="display:none">I was as frustrated by this book as I was addicted to it. Rosie and Alex were always in love with each other but never at the right place at the right time, both emotionally and physically. And neither would admit their feelings. I tore through the pages muttering under my breath that if the author did not make things right EVENTUALLY, I would lose it. I won't give anything away.<br /><br />I thought it was adorable that Rosie's daughter Katie had a relationship with a boy named Toby that completed mirrored Rosie and Alex's relationship except that Katie was always able to follow her dreams whereas the world kept slamming the door in Rosie's face over and over AND OVER again. It was sad, really, because Rosie was a great person - full of life, love, and humor.<br /><br />I loved the secondary characters, especially Stephanie (Rosie's sister)and Toby. There were parts of this book that were equally heartbreaking as humorous, but it came together in a way that made my heart swell.<br /><br />I really loved this book and highly recommend it to fans of chick lit and romantic comedy.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_42769399" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42769399" />
    <a title="Faith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1863114-faith"><img alt="Faith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231764582p2/1863114.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/42769399?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faith" href="/user/show/1863114-faith">Faith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1863114-faith?shelf=2006">2006</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42769399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18113411250828083591">[Why is the American title Love Rosie, when the original more poetic one is Where Rainbows End?:]<br/><br/>Rosie and Alex have been best friends ever since they were 5 years old. It takes them a million years to admit that they love each other. This is "My Best Friend's Wedding" dragged out on 450 pages. Very much a romantic comedy. A bad and boring romantic comedy. Does Cecilia Ahern not understand that everything does not have to happen in one book? After 50 pages I was already bored and started feeling</span>
  <span id="freeText18113411250828083591" style="display:none">[Why is the American title Love Rosie, when the original more poetic one is Where Rainbows End?:]<br /><br />Rosie and Alex have been best friends ever since they were 5 years old. It takes them a million years to admit that they love each other. This is "My Best Friend's Wedding" dragged out on 450 pages. Very much a romantic comedy. A bad and boring romantic comedy. Does Cecilia Ahern not understand that everything does not have to happen in one book? After 50 pages I was already bored and started feeling like the book was ready to end. But no. About a million more things happened to keep Rosie and Alex from admitting they love each other. I could easily have stopped reading, but I didn't, cos I wanted the right to say this book is crap... But I did skip a page or two here and there...<br /><br />And other thing that makes this book not work is the way the story is told. The book consists of notes, letters, emails and IM conversations. Usually I like this kind of change of the perspective, or rather, letters etc make me feel closer to the characters. But that is when there is a few passages like that in the book. 450 pages of them is too much. The way of telling the story leaves me cold. Since I only get the letters, the characters feel distant. <br /><br />Sorry, I'm never gonna read anything by Cecilia Ahern again. Being the daughter of the Irish prime minister and the sister of the wife somebody in Westlife doesn't make anybody a good writer. (I know that's a rude comment.)<br /><br />In short: more is not more, more is less.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18113411250828083591" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WcAILLssYLyCs+NNkKEvVYiQC3gNkpF4V/AHAh/7KA+paaif04fPRYE+cfMoPZsORZ3BKbdi9N5TBh/4u/nA5Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('16vN4KC/BWJtTLkmyObsuHC9dB6VZCJpbn8g0EHzG7MnAm1TyBSqm27BK5hweljjvbC+Ty+UR89qiTgq5fHzWQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

She takes a badly needed job working for ex–Master of the Universe Will Traynor, who is wheelchair bound after an accident. Will has always lived a huge life—big deals, extreme sports, worldwide travel—and now he’s pretty sure he cannot live the way he is.\n\nWill is acerbic, moody, bossy—but Lou refuses to treat him with kid gloves, and soon his happiness means more to her than she expected. When she learns that Will has shocking plans of his own, she sets out to show him that life is still worth living.\n\nA Love Story for this generation and perfect for fans of John Green’s The Fault in Our Stars, Me Before You brings to life two people who couldn’t have less in common—a heartbreakingly romantic novel that asks, What do you do when making the person you love happy also means breaking <span id="freeTextContainer14286068127647006735">Cecelia Ahern was born and grew up in Dublin. She is now published in nearly fifty countries, and has sold over twenty-five million copies of her novels worldwide. Two of her books have been adapted as films and she has created several TV series.</span>
